## Content
````
`packages\core\agent_framework\_workflows\_magentic.py` serves as a comprehensive framework for orchestrating workflows using multiple agents, particularly under the Magentic One system. The file facilitates complex interactions within workflows, leveraging Large Language Model (LLM)-powered managers to dynamically plan, execute, monitor, and adapt task sequences involving agents.

### Purpose and Functionality
The main objective of the file is to provide facilities for organizing, managing, and executing tasks using various agent protocols within pre-configured workflows. The code constructs workflows that handle task planning, progress assessments, human interventions, and final answer synthesis through well-defined structures and operations.

### Key Components and Execution
The file includes several classes that perform distinct yet interconnected roles:

- **`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticAgentExecutor`**: Enhances agent execution within workflows, integrating mechanisms for processing conversation flows, managing agent states, and addressing human intervention.
  
- **`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticBuilder`**: Implements a fluent API for configuring and building workflows with multiple agents, supporting customization in participant roles, management strategies, and enabling checkpointing and event callbacks.
  
- **`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticContext`**: Manages the context for interaction, storing attributes related to tasks, chat histories, and participant descriptions essential for tracking workflow states.
  
- **`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase`** and **`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.StandardMagenticManager`**: Define the abstract and standard implementations for managers handling LLM interactions, focusing on task orchestration through dynamic prompts and plan updates.
  
- **`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticOrchestratorExecutor`**: Facilitates orchestration logic within the Magentic One workflow, managing task ledger creation, agent coordination, reset, and replanning processes.
  
- **`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticWorkflow`**: A wrapper providing convenience methods for executing and managing workflows, supporting task initiation via various formats.
  
The file also includes several internal classes for constructing intervention requests, progress tracking, and task ledger management, such as `_MagenticHumanInterventionRequest`, `_MagenticTaskLedger`, `_MagenticProgressLedger`.

### Interactions and Dependencies
The file integrates extensively with other components within the `agent_framework`, utilizing modules for chat orchestration, message handling, and workflow contexts. It leverages base classes for execution and orchestration such as `BaseGroupChatOrchestrator`, and collaborates with external libraries for LLM integration through interfaces like `AgentProtocol`.

Dependencies include imports for functions and classes necessary for agent execution, message transformation, checkpointing, and orchestration processes. These elements ensure the coherent operation of workflows by guiding message exchanges and updating states dynamically within task contexts.

The framework's components collectively enable robust management and orchestrated execution of tasks across workflows, accommodating human interventions, and optimizing agent interactions through structured methodologies.
````

## Content
````
`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticAgentExecutor` is a specialized class designed to integrate agents into workflows with added capabilities for handling conversation flows and human intervention. It extends the functionality of an `Executor`, primarily focusing on managing the state and responses of agents within a task ledger context.

**Purpose and Functionality**: The class serves the purpose of facilitating agent participation in workflows by managing conversation states, handling requests and responses, and processing human interventions as part of tool approval workflows.

**Key Components and Execution**:
- **Initialization**: The constructor (`__init__`) accepts an agent conforming to `AgentProtocol` or `Executor`, and an `agent_id` string for identification.
- **Checkpoint Management**: Methods `on_checkpoint_save` and `on_checkpoint_restore` provide mechanisms to save and restore agent state, specifically focusing on chat history for execution continuity.
- **Message Handling**: Handlers such as `handle_response_message` and `handle_request_message` manage incoming messages, leveraging a workflow context to process specific agent tasks or user requests.
- **Tool Approval**: `handle_tool_approval_response` functions to process human responses to tool approval requests, categorizing actions into approval, rejection, or guidance modes.
- **Persona Role Determination**: `_get_persona_adoption_role` assesses the agent's capability to support SYSTEM messages and adjusts role adoption strategies accordingly.
- **Invocation**: `_invoke_agent` is a critical method, invoking wrapped agents and processing response updates. It streams responses and manages human input requests, only processing the first input request due to architectural constraints.

**Interactions and Dependencies**: The class integrates deeply with the `WorkflowContext`, utilizing its mechanisms to manage agent responses and communications. It depends on importing conversation state encoding and agent framework components to ensure proper operation. Local imports are utilized to address cycle dependencies.

Overall, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticAgentExecutor` orchestrates and augments agent capabilities within workflow environments by handling communication, managing execution states, and processing human interactions proficiently.
````

## Content
````
The class `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticBuilder` serves as a fluent builder to construct workflows for orchestrating multiple agents within the Magentic One framework. This framework leverages Large Language Model (LLM)-powered managers to coordinate agent activities, including dynamic task planning, progress tracking, and adaptive replanning. The class offers a fluent Application Programming Interface (API) allowing users to configure various aspects of the workflow, such as participants and managers, plan reviews, checkpointing, and event callbacks.

The purpose and functionality of this class are designed to facilitate the construction and execution of complex multi-agent orchestration workflows, allowing seamless integration between agents with diverse roles. The workflow is executed by invoking the `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticBuilder.build` method, which constructs and returns the configured workflow. Participants, represented by agents or executors, are added using the `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticBuilder.participants` method, and are crucial in executing tasks directed by the manager.

Critical components include various methods such as `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticBuilder.with_plan_review`, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticBuilder.with_human_input_on_stall`, and `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticBuilder.with_checkpointing`, each providing functionality enhancements like enabling human intervention for plan reviews and stalls, and executing checkpointing for workflow state persistence. These methods ensure workflows can pause for human evaluations, recover from failures, and save significant transitions.

The class interacts with other elements in the system, primarily integrating with agents like `agent_framework.ChatAgent` and managers such as `MagenticManagerBase` or `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.StandardMagenticManager`. It supports the creation of workflows using pre-configured managers or auto-creating managers with agents, leveraging prompts for various stages of task planning and execution. Prompts are customizable for extracting facts, generating plans, reassessing progress, synthesizing responses, and decision-making strategies.

Dependencies include various agent frameworks, LLM clients such as `azure.ai.projects.aio.AIProjectClient`, and storage implementations like `agent_framework.InMemoryCheckpointStorage`. These dependencies are integral for functionalities like manager creation and checkpoint storage.

Overall, the class is structured to guide users through the setup and execution of agent-centric workflows, extending capabilities to human interventions, customized management, and setting boundaries on task rounds and stall detection. The builder pattern allows modular workflow configurations, contributing to adaptable and robust orchestration within an intelligent agent coordination system.
````

## Content
````
The `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticContext` class serves as a comprehensive context management system for a "Magentic manager," designed to handle chat interactions and related attributes. This class is a subclass of `DictConvertible`, indicating that it possesses methods for converting instances to and from a dictionary representation. It encapsulates several attributes: 

- `task`: A `ChatMessage` object representing the current task or communication focus.
- `chat_history`: A list composed of `ChatMessage` objects, initialized with a `_new_chat_history` factory function to store the sequence of conversation.
- `participant_descriptions`: A dictionary with string keys and values initiated via the `_new_participant_descriptions` factory, detailing participant identities or roles.
- `round_count`, `stall_count`, and `reset_count`: Integer counters to track the number of conversation rounds, stalled interactions, and reset actions respectively.

The method `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticContext.to_dict()` facilitates the conversion of an instance into its dictionary form, while the class method `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticContext.from_dict()` reconstructs an instance from a dictionary, handling nested chat message payloads using the `_message_from_payload` function for individual message decoding.

The `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticContext.reset()` method is pivotal for reverting certain attributes to their initial states. Specifically, it clears `chat_history` and resets `stall_count`, incrementing `reset_count` each time it's invoked. Noteworthy is the persistence of `task`, `round_count`, and `participant_descriptions post-reset, maintaining continuity in the context's overarching handling.

This class likely integrates with systems responsible for managing chat workflows, depending on external procedures or functions like `_new_chat_history`, `_new_participant_descriptions`, and `_message_from_payload`, which are crucial for its operation. Its design enables the organized tracking and modification of chat session parameters, offering structured management throughout a conversation lifecycle.
````

## Content
````
The `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase` class serves as a foundational abstract base class for managing the Magentic One system, which appears to be involved in task orchestration or workflow management. It specifically defines the structure for derived classes to implement logic related to task planning, replanning, ledger creation, and final answer preparation in an asynchronous manner. 

The class constructor initializes three attributes: `max_stall_count`, `max_reset_count`, and `max_round_count`, which regulate the number of stalls, resets, and rounds allowed, respectively. These parameters can be tailored, providing flexibility for specific workflow needs. The class also contains an attribute named `task_ledger_full_prompt`, intended for type safety, and suggests that derived classes may override this attribute with specific string values.

Key methods of the class, marked as abstract, require implementation by subclasses. These methods include: `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase.plan`, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase.replan`, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase.create_progress_ledger`, and `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase.prepare_final_answer`. Each of these methods is essential for coordinating complex task management processes, allowing subclasses to define specific strategies for task planning and execution in a Magentic context.

Furthermore, the class provides two methods, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase.on_checkpoint_save` and `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase.on_checkpoint_restore`, prepared to handle the serialization and restoration of runtime state for checkpointing purposes, contributing to resilience and recovery capabilities in task management scenarios.

The class interacts with other components such as `MagenticContext` and `ChatMessage`, indicating dependencies on these data structures for representing context and communication messages, respectively. Additionally, `_MagenticProgressLedger`, connected with ledger creation, underscores the utility of progress tracking within workflows. The abstractions provided by `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticManagerBase` ensure that developers can build customized managers tailored to specific workflow purposes, leveraging asynchronous operations and state management principles.

## Content
````
The `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticOrchestratorExecutor` class is designed to manage the orchestration of tasks within the Magentic One workflow. It extends the `BaseGroupChatOrchestrator` and provides logic for task planning, progress tracking, agent coordination, and message routing. The class is responsible for orchestrating the workflow, including initial task ledger creation, handling human intervention requests, and resetting and replanning workflows when necessary. 

Key components of the class include attributes initialized in the constructor and various methods handling task orchestration processes. The attributes include dictionaries for registered agent executors and workflow context, task ledger, locks for serialization, flags for plan signoff requirements, and counters for plan reviews and initialization termination states. The constructor initializes these attributes and accepts parameters specifying whether plan signoff is needed, the maximum number of review rounds, whether stall interventions are enabled, and an optional executor ID.

Methods within the class perform specific tasks such as registering agent executors (`register_agent_executor`), emitting orchestrator messages to a workflow event stream (`_emit_orchestrator_message`), and handling checkpoint management (`on_checkpoint_save` and `on_checkpoint_restore`). The class also handles start messages with `handle_start_message`, initializing the orchestration process, sending plan review requests when human signoffs are needed, as well as engaging in inner and outer orchestration loops (`_run_inner_loop` and `_run_outer_loop`) for workflow coordination.

The `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticOrchestratorExecutor` class interacts with external elements such as agent executors, managers, and human interventions within the workflow. It coordinates with these dependencies to ensure the efficient progression of workflows and incorporates user inputs at critical junctions. It maintains backward compatibility with existing systems while integrating newer orchestration structures and methodologies.

Overall, this class is a pivotal element within the Magentic framework, orchestrating complex interactions and workflow management tasks with fidelity to the workflow dynamism and external dependencies involved.
````

## Content
````
The class `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticWorkflow` serves as a specialized wrapper around a base `Workflow` object, providing enhanced convenience methods for managing and executing magnetic workflows. This class is designed to facilitate the integration and operation of workflows within a broader system, accommodating task initiation via different input types.

### Purpose and Functionality
`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticWorkflow` allows users to interact with a `Workflow` object more efficiently. The class implements methods to initiate workflow execution using a task string or a task message, accommodating both asynchronous event streaming and complete event collection. It provides methods to execute workflows asynchronously while yielding workflow events over streams and methods gathering events into complete results.

### Key Components and Execution
The class includes methods such as `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticWorkflow.run_streaming_with_string`, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticWorkflow.run_streaming_with_message`, and their synchronous counterparts, `run_with_string` and `run_with_message`. These methods leverage existing workflow capabilities by converting different input types (`str` and `ChatMessage`) into a `_MagenticStartMessage`, initiating workflow runs asynchronously and allowing events to be collected or streamed.

The method `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticWorkflow._validate_checkpoint_participants` ensures the integrity of participant lists against workflow checkpoints before restoration, incorporating potential checkpoint loads from storage or `runner_context`.

### Interactions and Dependencies
`agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticWorkflow` largely relies on its underlying `Workflow`, delegated functionally through `__getattr__`, ensuring comprehensive access to its properties and methods. It depends on and interacts with components such as `_MagenticStartMessage`, `WorkflowEvent`, and `WorkflowCheckpoint`, integrating smoothly with event-driven asynchronous systems.

Together, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.MagenticWorkflow` efficiently orchestrates magnetic workflows within a potentially broader framework, optimizing interaction with task-based events, task messages, and checkpoint validations.

## Content
````
The `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.StandardMagenticManager` class serves as a specialized manager for handling Language Model (LM) interactions related to task orchestration. It extends from `MagenticManagerBase` and leverages language model abilities to orchestrate various task management steps like fact gathering, plan creation, progress tracking, and synthesizing final answers. This class is meticulously designed to mirror the original Magentic One orchestration process through explicit prompt definitions.

### Purpose and Functionality
The primary function of the `StandardMagenticManager` class is to systematically manage the orchestration of tasks using a collaborative language model through explicit prompts. This involves managing lifecycle events such as gathering initial facts, creating and updating plans, logging progress, and producing final synthesized outcomes. The standard manager ensures the prompts can be adjusted according to specific task needs while managing constraints like stall counts and execution retries.

### Key Components and Execution
The class is structured with critical attributes and methods designed for maintaining and updating the task ledger, providing a structured orchestration protocol:
- **Initialization**: The constructor initializes with configurable parameters for task management, including optional prompts for task steps, maximum thresholds for stalls, resets, and retries, establishing defaults if not provided.
- **Prompts**: Overridable prompt patterns facilitate contextual task orchestration steps, ensuring seamless model interaction.
- **Methods**:
  - `_complete`: A fundamental asynchronous method that interacts with the agent to execute messages and retrieve conversation completions.
  - `plan`: Initiates task planning, gathering facts, and constructing a plan, storing details in a task ledger.
  - `replan`: Adjusts the plan upon identifying execution stalls, refining facts and plans based on the current task context.
  - `create_progress_ledger`: Manages the creation of a JSON-formatted progress ledger ensuring error handling and retry capabilities.
  - `prepare_final_answer`: Synthesizes a final answer output from the task ledger.

### Interactions and Dependencies
The class interfaces heavily with the `AgentProtocol`, a presumed interface for LM agents tasked with running natural language interactions configured with specific parameters. It interacts with the `_MagenticTaskLedger` to maintain stateful information about the task and plans. The contextual data flow involves a `MagenticContext` that holds the task specification and participant information essential for dynamic prompt generation.

### Integration and Extensions
Overall, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic.StandardMagenticManager` presents an integration-oriented design, where the effective composition of message sequences and task ledger management guides action updates in task orchestration. Its cohesive utilization of agent models, persistence of orchestration states, and adaptive prompt handling ensure comprehensive lifecycle management of task-based conversations in AI-driven environments.
````

## Content
````
The class `agent_framework._workflows._magentic._MagenticHumanInterventionRequest` facilitates the generation of a structured request for human intervention within a Magentic workflow system. Its primary function is to manage scenarios where workflow processes require human input, categorizing the intervention under three types: plan review, tool approval, and stall. 

This class defines attributes pertinent to each intervention type. For plan review, attributes such as `task_text`, `facts_text`, `plan_text`, and `round_index` are designated to facilitate task assessment and feedback procedures. For tool approval, `agent_id`, `prompt`, `context`, and `conversation_snapshot` are included to describe and provide context for the input sought from a human agent, focusing on agent interactions and conversations. Within the stall intervention context, `stall_count`, `max_stall_count`, `stall_reason`, and `last_agent` detail the conditions under which workflows are stalled and the rationale for intervention.

The `request_id` serves as a unique identifier, using `uuid4()` for generating non-colliding IDs, to ensure correspondence clarity. The default values provided for `kind` and `kind` specific fields ensure the class can be readily utilized without requiring initial explicit assignments, promoting efficient instantiation.

Internally, the class utilizes Python data structures such as `str`, `int`, and `list`, along with `field` from the `dataclasses` module, assisting in attribute initialization, offering flexibility and simplification in managing default values and factory functions.

Furthermore, the class appears to rely on external constructs such as `MagenticHumanInterventionKind` and `ChatMessage`, indicating dependencies on predefined enumerated types and message structures, facilitating integration within broader systems containing these types.

Overall, `agent_framework._workflows._magentic._MagenticHumanInterventionRequest` acts as a crucial piece within Magentic systems, optimizing workflow-intervention requests for improved human-machine interaction and decision-making processes.
````

## Content
````
The class `agent_framework._workflows._magentic._MagenticStartMessage` is designed to facilitate the initialization of a magnetic workflow by encapsulating a set of chat messages. It inherits from `DictConvertible`, indicating an ability to convert its instances to and from dictionary representations. Its primary attribute `messages` holds a list of `ChatMessage` objects, which are created using the `_new_chat_message_list`.

The constructor method `__init__` accepts various formats for the messages parameter, such as a string, a `ChatMessage`, sequences thereof, or `None`. The messages undergo normalization through the `normalize_messages_input` function. If both `messages` and an optional `task` parameter yield empty results after normalization, the initialization raises a `ValueError`.

The `task` property retrieves the final user message designated as the task, implying the messages list is ordered with the task message always at the end.

`agent_framework._workflows._magentic._MagenticStartMessage.from_string` is a class method that facilitates the creation of an instance from a simple string representing the task message. Another class method, `from_dict`, constructs an instance from dictionary data, raising exceptions for invalid or missing keys.

The method `to_dict` provides a dictionary representation of the object, aligning with its inheritance of `DictConvertible`. The `messages` component in the dictionary undergoes particular verification to ensure it is a sequence, excluding string-like objects.

Interactions involve conversions between `ChatMessage` objects and their dictionary counterparts, indicating dependency on the `ChatMessage` class's functionality for message handling. The class integrates data representation skills with workflow initialization, demonstrating synchronous operations with message validation and transformation protocols.
````
